Causality and Created Things
intermediate
5 min
Al-Qattan and al-Qalanisi's Distinction Between Fi'l and Kalam
Al-Qattan and al-Qalanisi define fi'l and kalam to show fi'l can be from two agents.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will understand how al-Qattan and al-Qalanisi distinguish between general action (fi'l) and specific action (kalam) to answer the Mu'tazila objection.

Core Idea
Fi'l is a general term for anything brought about by power; kalam is a specific act requiring a unique locus.

In response to the Mu'tazila analogy, scholars like Abdullah ibn Sa'id al-Qattan and Abu al-Abbas al-Qalanisi pointed out that not all acts are like speech. They explained that 'fi'l' is a broad term applicable to anything that occurs by power, while 'kalam' is a specific type of act with special restrictions. This distinction allows them to affirm that an act can be attributed to both God and the servant without contradiction.

Guided Path
1
Read the response
Read the Arabic and translation of the response. Notice how they start by defining 'fi'l' and 'kalam' differently.
2
Compare the definitions
Fi'l is defined as a general name for everything possible and effected. Kalam is a specific act that negates silence and defect, requiring a single locus.
This difference is key to their argument.
3
Apply the distinction
Because fi'l is general, it can be attributed to multiple agents in different respects. Kalam cannot. Even kalam, as an act, can be from two agents but not as speech.
The hitting example illustrates that the same entity can be an act from one perspective and not from another.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ثم نظير هذا على قول من يسلم منكم أن العبد له فعل في الفرق بين فعل الفاعلين وكلام المتكلمين، فإن فعل العبد لما كان مخلوقا كان خلقا وفعلا الله تعالى فيكون فعلا الله تعالى وللعبد فيكون فعلا لفاعلين. فتدعى المعتزلة أن هذا محال، ويعتبرونه بكلام واحد أنه لا يكون كلاما لمتكلمين ويستحيل أن يكون ذلك فكذا هذا. أجابهم من سلم منكم أن للعبد فعلا وهو عبد الله بن سعيد القطان وأبو العباس القلانسي فقال: بأن الفعل اسم عام لكل ما هو مقدور مفعول، وقد ثبت أن فعلنا مقدور الله تعالى ومخلوقه فكان خلقه وفعله، والكلام اسم لفعل خاص وهو المعنى المنافي للسكوت والخرس والآفة، وهو ينافي سكوت المحل الذي قام به آفته ويستحيل قيامه بمحلين لنفي السكوت والآفة عن محلين فلم يكن كلاما لمحلين. فأما الفعل فهو اسم لما يقع بالقدرة وهو مقدور الله تعالى ومقدور العبد، فكان فعلا لهما، حتى إن الكلام لما كان يقع بقدرة الله خلقا وقدرة العبد كسبا كان أيضا فعلا لفاعلين أما لم يكن كلاهما لمتكلمين لما مر، فكذا الضرب عندنا لا يكون مضروبا لأنه اسم لنوع فعل وهو الإيلام والمضروب اسم للمتألم والضرب لا يقبل الألم فلم يكن مشروبا. فأما الضرب فإنه يقبل التخليق فكان مخلوقا مفعولا، فكان من حيث إنه فعل للعبد مفعولا لله تعالى، فأما من حيث إنه ضرب لم يكن مضروبا. ثم نحن إنما ندعي إحالة كون الفعل مفعولا لمن هو فعله، وإحالة كون المفعول فعلا لمن هو مفعوله وننكر اتحاد الفعل والمفعول وفيها ألزمت الأمر بخلافه، فإن فعل العبد عندنا كان مفعولا الله تعالى لا للعبد، وكان هو فعلا للعبد لا الله تعالى فمن كان هو فعلا له لم يكن مفعولا، ومن كان مفعولا له لم يكن فعلا له ونحن لا ننكر هذا وإنما ننكر اتحاد الفعل والمفعول بجهة واحدة وهو إضافته.
Then the parallel to this, according to the statement of one among you who concedes that the servant has an act, regarding the distinction between the act of two agents and the speech of two speakers: for the act of the servant, when it is created, is creation and act of God, so it is an act of God and of the servant, thus it is an act of two agents. Misconception & Correction
Misconception: One might think that fi'l and kalam are the same type of action, so the Mu'tazila analogy stands.
Correction: Al-Qattan and al-Qalanisi show that fi'l is a broader category than kalam. Kalam has special restrictions that do not apply to all acts.

Checkpoint
According to al-Qattan and al-Qalanisi, why can 'fi'l' be attributed to two agents but 'kalam' cannot?
A) Because 'fi'l' is created by God while 'kalam' is created by the servant.
B) Because 'fi'l' is a general term for anything brought about by power, while 'kalam' is a specific act requiring a single locus.
C) Because 'fi'l' is a physical act and 'kalam' is a mental act.
D) Because the Mu'tazila misunderstood the definition of 'kalam'.

Key Takeaway
Fi'l is a general term for what occurs by power, while kalam is a specific act with unique constraints; this distinction allows an act to be from two agents without contradiction.

How This Lesson Applies — to MY Life?
?
When you reflect on your daily actions, do you truly see them as both created by God and acquired by you? How does this dual attribution affect your sense of responsibility and your humility before God? Will you pause this week to acknowledge God's role in even your smallest acts?
?
The passage emphasizes that speech cannot be from two speakers. The Quran is God's speech. Have you ever considered that your own speech, when it aligns with truth, is a reflection of that divine speech yet also your own? How does this distinction challenge you to speak with greater care and accountability? What one change will you make in your speech today?
?
Al-Qattan and al-Qalanisi use the example of hitting to show different aspects of an act. When you hurt someone or cause pain, do you consider the 'hit' as your act but the suffering as something God creates? How does this realization affect your repentance and your efforts to avoid harm? Will you seek forgiveness from God and the person you've harmed this week?
